Sports Jiangsu Education Department's Public Sports Inspectors Depart, 15th Meeting to Formulate Inspection Points 225

The Jiangsu Education Department dispatched personnel to inspect public sports in various counties. The department convened a discussion with various inspectors yesterday (the 15th) at 3:00 PM, including Wu Bangwei, Xiang Jutan, Zhang Zhenfan, Yuan Zhonglian, Xu Xiaochuan, Yuan Jidong, Pei Xiyuan, and Liu Baichuan, totaling eight people. Xiang Jutan chaired. First, the chairman reported on the past management of sports grounds in various counties, the Education Department's approach to rectifying sports grounds, and the significance of this inspection. Then, the matters to be paid attention to during the inspection and inspection methods were discussed, and a set of inspection points for sports grounds in various counties was formulated. After the discussion, they departed separately for inspection. The inspection points are as follows:

Inspection Points (A) Site Equipment: (1) Is the location suitable? What is the environment like? (2) How much equipment is there? Is it suitable for the needs of the local public? (3) What are the improvement methods for the overall layout? (B) Expenditure and Receipts: (1) What is the monthly expenditure? What percentage do salaries and operating expenses account for? Is it in compliance with regulations? (2) Are monthly revenues and expenditures disclosed? Can waste be avoided? (3) Are there fee payment methods for athletes throughout the ground? If there are fee payment regulations, is there any impact? (C) Organization and Management: (1) Is the organization practical? (2) Is the management strict? Is the agreement not implemented? (3) Are the qualifications of the staff accurate? Is the work diligent? Are there any dual positions? (D) Business Progress: (2) Has a sports training class been organized? How many of the five types of Chinese martial arts, calisthenics, apparatus exercises, track and field, and ball techniques have been formed? Are the above five types suitable for the interests and needs of the public? Are there other training organizations? What are the results of the organization and training? (The number of participants in various training sessions and dropouts must be recorded in detail.) (2) Has a competition been held? Has an amateur sports meet been held? How many of the seven types of football, basketball, weightlifting, shuttlecock, jump rope, walking, and ping pong have been held? Are there other athletic competitions held? What are the results of the competition? (The number of participants and results of various competitions must be recorded in detail.) What kind of sport is the local public best at? (3) Is there adequate equipment and organization for women's and children's sports? Is there a fixed time each day to specifically guide women's and children's sports? What kind of teaching materials are used? How many participants are there? (4) Has a children's health competition been held? What are the methods and results? (The children participating in the competition and the results must be recorded in detail.) (5) What plans are there for hygiene sports? What practical work is there? (6) Has the organization of the Sports Association been attempted? What is the process and the result? (7) Is there an affiliated people's school? How many levels are there? How many students are there? Is there sports training in the curriculum? What teaching materials are used? What are the students' feelings? (8) Has a physical examination been held? How many people have been tested? What are the results? (9) What special local folk games are there in this county? Have any attempts been made to adopt or improve them? (10) Are there any unsanitary customs in this county? Have any attempts been made to correct them?

Jiaotong University Student Assaults Referee: Shen Huichun Suffers Serious Injuries to Left Ear and Waist; Hearing Loss Feared Due to Excessive Bleeding in Left Ear; Shen Reports Facts to Referee Association, Seeks Intervention 226

On Saturday, during the Jiangda Football Match between Jinan University and Jiaotong University at Jiaotong University, an incident occurred where a Jiaotong University student assaulted referee Shen Huichun. Details were reported yesterday. The sports community is extremely indignant about this matter, particularly dissatisfied with Jiaotong University's sports director, Shen Guoquan, and the team members' inaction, failing to fulfill their duty to protect the referee. The following is a compilation of expressions from various parties yesterday and details of Mr. Shen's injuries.

Mr. Shen's General Condition 227

According to Mr. Shen, he was immediately assaulted and injured on the field. After the crowd dispersed, he drove himself to Tongren Hospital for treatment. Due to the severity of his injuries, he stayed at the hospital that night. His left ear was severely injured with significant blood loss. Doctors said he might lose his hearing. His right waist was also seriously injured, causing extraordinary pain. He received immediate medication and bandaging. This morning, he followed the doctor's advice to leave the hospital for light movement to facilitate blood circulation and prevent stagnation. However, due to the inability to exert strength in his waist, walking was particularly inconvenient.

Subjected to Cold Remarks and Sarcasm 228

Mr. Shen also said that when he was beaten to the ground, if Chen Bingde had not dragged him up and Jinan University's goalkeeper, Ye Peichu, and Mr. Tu Kaiyuan had not protected him and taken him to the gymnasium, his life would have been in danger. However, after arriving at the gymnasium, he was subjected to cold remarks and sarcasm from the Jiaotong University team staff. When leaving the school gate, Jiaotong University's sports director, Shen Guoquan, not only did not express any apology but questioned, "This penalty kick should not have been called." He stated, "Whether this penalty should have been awarded is something I don't need to argue. Those who are discerning will understand. For Mr. Shen, as the director of sports at a university, to say such a thing speaks volumes about his moral character."

Negotiation by Referee Association 229

Mr. Shen further stated that this morning (i.e., yesterday), Shen Guoquan, after seeing the harsh criticism of Jiaotong University in the newspapers, realized he was in the wrong. He went to the Sports Advancement Association to inquire about Mr. Shen's address and then visited his home, seemingly wanting to reconcile. Mr. Shen told Mr. Shen Guoquan that since he had hired the referee through the Sports Referee Association, not directly, and that Mr. Shen's refereeing was based on the Referee Association's appointment, he and Mr. Shen Guoquan could not negotiate directly. Mr. Shen could only report the facts to the Referee Association and let them resolve the matter. However, he was very grateful for Mr. Shen Guoquan's visit and concern.

Mr. Zhou Jiaqi's Remarks 230

Mr. Zhou Jiaqi, an official of the National Sports Advancement Association, is also an alumnus of Jiaotong University and has been a sports instructor at Jiaotong University for many years. He has always valued the spirit of sportsmanship. Mr. Zhou was also at the stadium that day. According to Mr. Zhou, Shen Guanlan's collision with Xu Yahui should have been penalized. Near the end of the second half, Jiaotong University students already displayed inappropriate behavior, seemingly indicating a willingness to resort to violence. Shen Guoquan, standing nearby, smiled knowingly. As expected, after the match, Mr. Shen was beaten. However, Shen Guoquan and the Jiaotong University players did not step forward to help, which was truly inappropriate. Mr. Shen Guoquan should have escorted Mr. Shen into the gymnasium after the match. If he had, the students would not have dared to cause trouble. Mr. Shen Guoquan's failure to do so only encouraged the students to be even more reckless.

Mr. Yu Hengzhi's Remarks 231

Mr. Yu Hengzhi, the director of sports at Jinan University, stated that he, having seen repeated disputes in university football matches, tried hard that day to prevent the players from playing roughly. However, the Jiaotong University players made many illegal collisions that day. When Xu Yahui was hurt by an opponent's collision, he protested to the referee, who sternly reprimanded him, saying, "Don't say too much, or you will be penalized and sent off." (According to referee Shen yesterday, he did say this). At one point, he was extremely indignant about the opponent's actions and truly wanted to instruct his school's players to retaliate in the same way. However, he knew that this was not proper behavior and would only lead to accidents. Therefore, he consistently forbade the players from being rough. During the halftime break, Xu Yahui expressed his feelings to Mr. Yu, who sternly reprimanded him, saying that he must continue to play as usual and not say too much. He felt that it was extremely unfortunate that referee Shen was beaten afterward.

Chen Bingde Also Injured 232

Mr. Chen Bingde, the director of sports at Fudan University, was also present and was the first to help Mr. Shen. According to Mr. Chen, after Mr. Shen was beaten to the ground, he immediately picked Mr. Shen up and, with the help of two others (Jinan University's goalkeeper Ye Peichu and Mr. Tu Kaiyuan), protected him into the stadium. However, as a result, Mr. Chen's back was also injured by Jiaotong University students, and he still feels the pain. When the crowd was attacking, in order to rescue Mr. Shen, Mr. Chen used a leather case for a camera lens (which resembled a pistol holster) as if it were a gun and sternly ordered the crowd to disperse. In reality, Mr. Chen did not have a gun and successfully tricked the crowd. This was truly an interesting anecdote from that day's chaos.

(1) Date: From the 20th of this month to the end of the month, every Wednesday and Saturday afternoon starting at 3:00 PM. (2) System: Single round-robin system. (3) Rules: According to the competition rules of the National Games. (4) Venue: If the home game is scheduled to be held at School A this year, it will be held at School B next year. (5) Referee: Hired by the home team with the consent of the visiting team. (6) Postponement: If there is rain or special circumstances and a request for a postponement, the other party must be consulted first, but the makeup game must not be later than the end of this month. Afterwards, the Mixed Team's morale was scattered, and the All Blacks' fighting power was also reduced due to Jia Youliang's injury. Finally, the All Blacks won 4 to 1 and won the Dayong Cup presented by the Dayong Rubber Company. In terms of the strength of the two teams, the forwards were strong, and the Mixed Team's talent was average, but it lacked coordination. The All Blacks were the opposite. From this comparison, it can be seen that cooperation is important in football matches.

Essays

On Children's Family Education 247

— Shen Yan

For a certain period, my neighbor was a Japanese family. The man was a low-level printing worker. There were only the husband and wife and three small children at home, not even a female servant. After the man went out, the woman cleaned and swept at home, working non-stop every minute. Therefore, her house was truly spotless and very clean. This naturally made me admire her greatly. However, these situations may also be seen in Western families. What is most impressive is the family education of the children. Just two examples are enough to make us Chinese feel ashamed.

The first is teaching children politeness. Every afternoon around three or four o'clock, the Japanese elementary school would dismiss its students. As usual, I could always hear a gentle and loud knock on the door. So I would look out from the window upstairs, and I would always see the woman walk out with a smiling face to open the door. As soon as the door opened, I would see three small heads simultaneously bow down, each making a ninety-degree bow. Then the oldest child would go in front, the second in the middle, and the youngest at the end, walking in order. But they were not stiff or slow, and their attitude was very lively. Seeing such orderly and respectful behavior really made people feel that the Japanese were unattainable!

The second is to instill patriotic ideas into children's small minds as much as possible. One day, it was probably some kind of Tenchōsetsu-like holiday. As usual, the family put on new clothes and hoisted a sun flag on the drying platform. They celebrated at home in the morning, singing the national anthem. In the afternoon, the husband and wife went out to participate in some gathering, and the three small children carried small sun flags to play in the alley. Later, somehow the youngest child accidentally broke a corner of the flag. The two older children saw it and hurried over to scold him. The oldest girl even asked my niece for some paste to repair the small national flag and carefully took it back home. According to what she told my niece, breaking the national flag would result in the most severe punishment from their parents.

From the above two points, it is a matter of course that the Japanese are strong. Their success is largely due to family education. Therefore, I feel that we must do our best to give our children appropriate family education and cannot dump the responsibility of educating children entirely on the shoulders of the teachers in the schools. You must know that if children are not given considerable family education, the result will not only affect the happiness of the family, but it will also be greatly related to the future of the country!

Servants 248

— Fu Yizhi

Servants seem to be a kind of easy job. They don't need the great strength of burden-bearing laborers, nor do they need the skills of operating machines. In particular, they don't need to hold an abacus, calculate profits and losses, or dip a brush in ink and stretch paper to write some "policy essays." They just need to understand the master's personality, know the master's likes and dislikes, serve diligently, and obey orders. If the master is in danger, they need to show a brave, desperate, and protective demeanor within the possible range. This is enough to qualify as a servant. Maybe after the master trusts them, they can have the hope of being promoted to another level.

However, this refers to the former family members, book boys, and the current so-called attendants, errand boys, and other personal servants. If they are serving in a group, it is not so simple and easy. For example, a tea server in a school or a company: the president, dean, and department heads of a university are often contemporary "celebrities" and naturally have their own personal errand boys. The presidents or general managers of well-capitalized companies are a kind of person standing at the highest level of society. In particular, there are very

Casual Talk on Cartoons 249

— Written by Qian Yun and Drawn by Wen Dongliang

Many married friends call the unmarried people children. Actually, what use is it to marry a wife? Women in the city just have to curl their hair and redden their lips to smile at you. They are very willing for their husbands to be like their pet dogs. If you are happy, you might as well hold them down and spank their little butts. They will automatically come to kiss you. It is said that modern couples play this kind of trick, and people will say they are fashionable.

High or extremely clever private servants. We can ignore them. If in ordinary schools and ordinary companies, there are only tea rooms for public use. Every teacher has the right to order this tea server around. No matter how obedient, hardworking, and not lazy he is, there will always be places where the supply is insufficient. When Mr. Zhang calls him to go to do something, Mr. Li calls him but he doesn't respond, which is a bit unpleasant. Conversely, Mr. Zhang will also blame him. I think there is nothing more thankless than this in the world.

But, if you are experienced and worldly, and also clever, you can be competent and happy. That all depends on your ability to measure the power of the teachers. Even something as small as arranging dishes for a meal must be done according to this standard. For example, if there are the president, the dean of academic affairs, the dean of student affairs, and other directors and teachers at the table, or the general manager, manager, sales director, accountant, and other small employees in a company, then the most expensive and palatable dish, "Winter Mushrooms and Half-Singing," should be placed on the side of the president's or general manager's seat. The second most expensive should be placed on the side of the next most powerful person. Inferior dishes may be placed in front of the "inferior" teachers or small employees. If you are called to do something at the same time, do it according to this standard. If the callers are teachers with equal power, then you must weigh the urgency. If the caller has no power, you may make excuses about being too busy, anyway, they can't do anything to you.

This secret was recently observed from the actions of a person with more than ten years of tea server history. However, by referring to other sources, it was discovered that this secret has a wide range of applications. There are many people who have gained both fame and fortune by possessing it. It is not only servants who do this. I have to attribute it to my own backwardness!

Marriage 250

— Yu Youqing

In the past few days, on the streets of Suzhou, several large hotels have been decorated with lanterns and streamers, used as wedding halls. There are modern-style weddings, and there are also brides who cover their faces with red scarves, not diminishing the ceremonies of the Qing Dynasty. Whether new-style or old-style, holding a wedding in the Western wind feels somewhat sweet and profoundly interesting.

Who says marriage is the tomb of love? Seeing pairs of happy couples, they are not all people in tombs! Originally, on cold nights where the water is cool and the lonely quilt is not warm, having two people sleep together in the same bed reduces some of the cold. Especially the newly married couple, it's very flavorful. Therefore, in the small spring weather of the abolished calendar, hotels are borrowed as wedding halls, perhaps because of the climate, which makes people have to pair up single men and women.

Old-fashioned marriage brings together a pair of men and women who don't know each other, and they bow to each other in public. Their future destiny is truly in the unknown. However, old-fashioned marriage still holds some viewpoints under the control of old etiquette. It is said that if you marry a chicken, you follow the chicken; if you marry a dog, you follow the dog. For everything in the future, they mostly endure each other. If we talk about modern-style marriage, I am somewhat afraid, because if the man has no wealth and the woman has no beauty, I'm sorry, it won't take long for problems to arise. They see marriage as a play, and they separate and go their separate ways.

I saw the electric candles shining brightly and the wedding hustle and bustle in the hotel, but when I turned around, I saw on the counter of a paper shop, on the cover of the XX Daily, an announcement by lawyer XXX representing XXX's divorce from Ms. XX. I couldn't help but shudder. Marriage really seems like a play.

Gui Zhi laughed, covering her mouth, upon hearing this. Madam Jiang found a box of matches and handed it to Elder Zhao. After these days, once Zi Qiang's letter arrives, I'll be busy. There won't be time for joy." As he said this, he held a cigarette, tapping it against the case. Women's Paradise

Housewife's Must-Know Laundry Knowledge 252

— Pei Mei

Washing Gloves

As the weather gets colder, gloves are a necessity for warmth. It's worth knowing various facts about gloves. Here are some simple and effective methods to make gloves last longer. Why not give them a try?

To wash exquisite white kid gloves, first put the gloves on your hands. Then, use a small piece of flannel dipped in hot flour and rub it vigorously. Pay special attention to the thumbs and between the fingers. After rubbing vigorously for a while, use a good, stiff brush to brush away the flour particles. The gloves will be like new without any damage.

For soiled colored gloves and white sheepskin gloves, there is a simple way to make them like new. Place them in a wide-necked bottle filled with plenty of gasoline. After putting the gloves in, seal the bottle with a stopper and gently shake it once. After shaking, let it sit for several hours, then take them out, wipe the gloves with a dry cloth, and place them in a cool place to let the gasoline evaporate completely. Soiled gloves, after this washing, can be refreshed. Moreover, this bottle of gasoline can be used repeatedly without needing to be replaced after each wash, which is very economical.

The best way to wash brown sheepskin gloves is to use hot milk with a little shredded soap or soap powder dissolved in it. First, lay the gloves flat on a thick towel. Then, use a small piece of flannel dipped in hot milk with dissolved soap to wipe them. Finally, straighten the fingers of the gloves, flatten the palms, and hang them in a ventilated place to dry.

To wash black sheepskin gloves, use a solution of equal parts good black shoe polish and pure olive oil mixed together. The best way to wash chamois leather gloves is in soapy foam (commonly known as soapy water, usually made by dissolving soap powder). This soapy foam is made with soap flakes or soap powder and a pint (unit of volume) of borax to soften the boiling water. After washing in soapy foam, wash several times in lukewarm water with a few drops of olive oil added. For each wash, change the water until it is clean. This way of washing will prevent chamois leather from hardening.

Washing Clothes

The quickest and most effective way to wash small woolen items or woolen clothes is to put them in a strainer with many small holes at the bottom. This strainer is placed in a container filled with warm soapy foam. First, press the woolen fabric or clothes tightly against the inner walls of the strainer and rub vigorously. Then, wash them several times in lukewarm water. After washing, press them against the inner walls of the strainer, trying to squeeze out as much water as possible. Only then should they be spread out on a flat surface, such as a table or a washboard. Be careful not to stretch or pull them tight when spreading them out. While drying, turn them over from time to time. Before washing colored fabrics, it is best to soak them thoroughly in cold water with plenty of salt added. This way, the colors will not fade during washing. If this precautionary step is not taken, the colors will definitely be damaged. However, if the colors are damaged, they can be restored. Simply use a sponge dipped in a mixture of equal parts household vinegar and cold water to moisten the colored fabrics. To prevent flannel from becoming stiff or felted after washing, simply add a little olive oil to the final rinse water. One tablespoon of olive oil per gallon of water is sufficient. If colored women's silk stockings are soaked overnight in warm soapy foam with a few drops of turpentine added before washing, they will not fade. One tablespoon of turpentine per quart (unit of volume) of soapy water is enough.

Before ironing or pressing fabrics or clothes, it is best to moisten them. The old method of spraying water with the mouth or sprinkling by hand is not very convenient. Now there are sprinklers made of tinplate or brass on the market. If you want an economical solution, you can use a glass bottle with a cork stopper. Just carve a small groove on one side of the cork to replace sprinkling water with your fingers.

One Year Editor 254

It has been exactly one year since the publication began last year on this day. Over the past year, we have received the support and promotion from both the medical and pharmaceutical communities, for which we are very grateful, especially to the gentlemen who have served as writers. In their busy schedules, whether in severe cold or sultry heat, they have wielded their pens to write, adding much color to this publication. This spirit of hard work encourages us to strive and forge ahead, and we should work even harder.

However, looking back at the state of the medical and pharmaceutical community in our country compared to last year, it is still generally chaotic with no progress; while in foreign countries, such as Japan and the Soviet Union, there are often new discoveries and inventions. What we should feel sad about is that others are already using science to deal with us, while we are still discussing whether science is needed, which truly breaks our hearts!

A year has passed quickly, and I hope there will be some progress next year.

A Few Words on the First Anniversary of This Publication 255

— Pang Jing Zhou

This publication has been around for fifty-two issues, which is just one year. So, we are publishing a "First Anniversary Special Issue." Jing Zhou has been entrusted by the editor-in-chief to say a few words. And as a fervent supporter of this publication, I cannot but speak!

The purpose of this publication is nothing more than to promote the true meaning of scientific medicine and pharmacy, and to instill common health knowledge. That was already stated by the editor at the time of publication. Now that we have worked for a year according to this purpose, we should think about whether this publication has fulfilled its duty. On this point, I believe it has been proven that this publication can be declared innocent! Why? Because when this publication reached its twentieth to thirtieth issue, Jing Zhou proposed that an advertisement be placed in this publication to solicit readers' opinions and criticisms as much as possible. This advertisement ran for five or six issues, and the result was that no criticism was received, which shows that everything in this publication has been tacitly approved by the public, which is also the fulfillment of this publication's duty.

Secondly, we must estimate the effects achieved by the work of this publication over the past year. On this point, there are completely numerical figures that can be calculated. Most newspaper readers know that Shen Bao has a daily circulation of 150,000 copies. Of course, the circulation of each issue of this publication is also 150,000 copies, because this publication is attached to the main newspaper and is not published in any local supplement! In China today, each newspaper is read by an average of ten people, so each issue's text is instilled into one million brains. Fifty-two issues a year means 52 million impressions into people's eyes. This huge number, written horizontally, actually requires six zeros after the 52. A smart person, after hearing Mei Lanfang's Farewell My Concubine once, will often learn his line, "碧海青天夜夜心" (bì hǎi qīng tiān yè yè xīn - green sea, blue sky, night after night, my heart). Since the audience of this publication is as many as 52 million times, it can be equivalent to Dr. Mei singing for 10,000 days at the Tianchan Stage (which can accommodate about 5,000 people), which is equivalent to singing for twenty-seven and a half years. As I think about it, probably many people can not only recite "green sea, blue sky, night after night, my heart," but also "Su San leaves Hongtong County" and "Wang Baochuan lowers her head and looks with her eyes" will also be fluent. Thus, it can be inferred that the truth of new medicine has been able to penetrate people's minds. If it is also like today's Peking Opera, passed from one person to ten, from ten people to a hundred, becoming a common practice, and everyone likes a few lines, then can the progress of Chinese medical affairs not be expected immediately? This is what this publication is very fortunate for.

However, although the positive articles say so, when we think about the reverse side, how can we know that the readers' lack of criticism of this publication is not the indifference of society to medical and pharmaceutical issues? How can we know that the readers do not read the newspaper, first look at the Northeast Peace Talks, and first look at the Fujian Incident, and feel that this publication is not worth a glance? How can we know that the readers do not spend the time reading this publication on watching Farewell My Concubine?

Even if it is really calculated according to the above numbers, then we must also think that the total number of people in the country is 400 million. For 400 million people, listening to the opera only 52 million times a year is equivalent to eight people listening only once a year. Can it be considered universal? We also have to compare this publication with Hollywood's famous movie films. One film is made into hundreds of copies and shown in major cities around the world for several weeks. How many viewers are there?

Alas! Thinking of this, I cannot help but shout, "This publication has not yet succeeded, comrades still need to work hard!"

A Humble Word to the Gentlemen Presiding Over the Beggar Relief Association 256

— Wang Qi Zhang

On the 25th of last month, Shanghai newspapers reported on the Second Meeting of the Beggar Relief Association, stating that there are approximately 30,000 beggars in this city, requiring an annual expenditure of one million for relief purposes. Truly, they regard the people as if they were wounded, a benevolent intention. I humbly believe that charitable undertakings originate from compassion, and compassion, in turn, is rooted in the shared sympathy of humankind. Only those philanthropists who can truly practice their benevolence must first sympathize with their own families, and then extend that sympathy to others, so that their kindness can benefit all living beings. For those who can truly wear out their heels and save others from hardship are few and far between. In simple terms, if one's own self, family, and clan cannot achieve warmth and sustenance, they certainly cannot spare a thought for the warmth and sustenance of others. Only when one's own self, family, and clan are first free from becoming beggars can they then help others who are beggars. Therefore, charitable undertakings originate from the shared sympathy of humankind, but whether that sympathy can achieve the purpose of permanent relief depends on the methods of relief. According to human abilities, although they differ, self-preservation and the love of life and fear of death are common traits. The descent of a person into beggary, even if it cannot be attributed entirely to the results of poor governance, is largely caused by family and social environment. A small portion may be weak individuals who have failed in their careers, and there may also be those who have fallen into pessimistic behavior due to setbacks in life. However, tracing the fundamental cause, it all stems from ignorance of economics and the inability to balance production and consumption on a material level. On this point, we can temporarily average and reorganize for them, but we cannot permanently bear the burden of supporting them. Therefore, relief methods should correct the error of imbalanced production and consumption, and strictly avoid taking on the responsibility of covering their imbalanced production and consumption. Those in the country who call themselves charitable mostly focus on bearing the burden of consumption and neglect planning for production. Therefore, the more relief there is, the more beggars there are; the more relief there is, the more the recipients become lazy. This is the most incomplete aspect of charitable undertakings, what is called sinking deeper and deeper and making a fool of oneself. The reason a person is a person is that they must have the inherent ability to support themselves. From scholars and officials to sedan chair carriers and footmen, unless they are tired, crippled, or ill, they should have the ability to act. Otherwise, they are simply cutting themselves off from food and clothing. However, those both above and below are ill with laziness. If the propertied class is lazy, they lose their property; if the bankrupt class is lazy, they fall into beggary. Moreover, in addition to laziness, is there not also the help or connivance in their begging and theft? In this way, if sympathy flows with such currents, giving money to the beggar will only make the donor and his family unhappy, and it is no different from planting the seeds of begging, theft, and evil. How can this be allowed? Therefore, the gentlemen presiding over the Beggar Relief Association, having shown great compassion and benevolence, and wishing to add to the care of the destitute and helpless poor, must first identify the goals, taking nourishing their livelihood and restoring their labor as the priority, and should absolutely not take on the burden of their consumables as their responsibility. Then, the 30,000 beggars in this city may be gradually reduced, and the annual expenditure of one million yuan may be used to make them self-reliant. Therefore, I propose several points for the gentlemen's reference.

(1) First, investigate how each individual has fallen into beggary and the reasons for it, classify and record them, and prepare them for teaching and observing their character for use.

(2) Divide them into elderly, adult, youth, and young children, and assess their physical strength and abilities, teaching them methods of production. Those who are ill should be treated in hospitals, and those who are disabled should be sent to homes for the disabled for care, demonstrating the idea that those who do not work will not eat.

(3) At the beginning of teaching methods of production, food and clothing should be provided by the government. When the methods are mastered, they should be self-sufficient. The remainder should be saved for them. Once they are successful, their independence should be maintained so they can re-enter society as people, and they should be rewarded regularly.

According to the English name of the association, Shanghai Anti-beggar Committee, it is clear that it is intended to resist and prevent begging, not to support it. Thus, the traditional concept of charity must be changed in order to have a proper appearance.

Heresies are refuted, and heresies flee. How prosperous, the truth that is marked.

Winter Child Hygiene 258

— Zhou Jun Chang

The severe cold has arrived, and if we want to maintain the health and happiness of children, we should pay special attention to them. Here are a few points for the reference of those who love their children.

(1) Fresh Air and Sunlight Fresh air and sunlight are necessities for making children strong and healthy. Sunlight that has passed through glass or clothing is of no help. It must be directly exposed to the body to help development and prevent rickets. Therefore, even on cold days, children should still play outdoors in the sunlight and absorb plenty of fresh air. If it is windy or rainy, dress them in warmer clothes and let them play indoors, but all windows must be open.

(2) Winter Clothing Children should wear more clothes in winter, but not too thick, because it can make active children sluggish. Therefore, they can wear less clothing indoors and add light and warm outerwear when going out. Wool outerwear and leggings are most suitable for wearing when playing.

(3) Quarterly Diet There must be plenty of nutritious food every day, but it should be known that children in winter do not need to eat more than in summer. In addition, attention should be paid to having sufficient beverages every day.

Page 14

(4) Bathing Bathing in cold weather is as necessary as in warm weather. If the bathroom is warm, there is no fear of catching a cold. Bathing every day and massaging their bodies can make their skin smooth and increase resistance.

(5) Afternoon Nap Daily afternoon naps are very beneficial to the health of young children. Older children can be replaced with rest. Children who have enough rest can reduce various crying and anger.

Inappropriate Inquiries for Illnesses and Requests for Medicines (Continued) 259

— Pang Jing Zhou

(B) Specific Parts

(1) Nervous system

One perception (clear or confused). Two headaches, dizziness. Three sleep. Four tremors. Five delirium (voice changes). Six reflexes (pupil reflexes, etc.). Seven Various disorders on sensory and motor nerves.

(2) Digestive system

One lips, tongue. Two larynx, uvula, tonsils. Three appetite. Four thirst. Five vomiting. Six bowel movements. Seven examine and palpate the abdomen (whether there are scars, depressions, whether there is pain on pressing, whether there are tumors). Eight percussion of the abdomen (whether there is gas, edema, whether there are tumors, nodules). Also percuss whether the liver and spleen are normal. Nine examine gastric juice and stool.

(3) Respiratory system

One chest structure. Two whether breathing is even. Three breathing movements (fast, slow, manner, sufficient, biased to one side, etc.). Four cough, choking, and sputum. Five symptoms obtained by percussion. Six symptoms obtained by auscultation. Seven chest fremitus and bronchial accessory sounds.

(4) Circulatory system

One observation of the heart area. Two observation of major blood vessels. Three palpation of heartbeat. Four palpation of the apex beat. Five percussion of the heart's position and size. Six auscultation of heart sounds. Seven listening to the sounds of the great arteries.

(5) Urine

One voluntary urination or bedwetting, whether there is pain. Two total amount in 24 hours. Three specific gravity. Four color clarity. Five acidity or alkalinity. Six whether there are proteins and sugar. Seven what the precipitate contains.

Looking at the above conditions, if you are just learning to diagnose diseases, in addition to the patient's gender and age, you need to check three parts, thirteen items, and sixty-five detailed items. However, in the medical profession's habit of diagnosing diseases, there is naturally no such trouble. Relying on experience, you can naturally use a simplified method to check the key points to diagnose a disease. However, on the other hand, there are many pains. Even if every item is checked, you may not get a definite diagnosis, and you must continue to examine the stool, urine, cough, discharge, etc. Or look at how his condition progresses. Some people also use an anal mirror, uterine mirror, laryngeal mirror, bladder mirror, and other instruments to examine. Even using X-rays for fluoroscopy. In short, diagnosing a disease can be extremely difficult and extremely complex. It is definitely not as simple as those letters from ordinary people asking for medicine. You can get a proper treatment. Not to mention anything else, just the patient not meeting the doctor, then the "examination" in the diagnostic elements cannot be resolved. Only using a part of the "chief complaint," that is, according to the old doctor's saying, looking, listening, asking, and feeling, only one word of asking is done. Isn't it too far off topic? Therefore, I think that asking for illness and asking for medicine is extremely inappropriate. If you really want to arouse the reader's medical and pharmaceutical interests, there seem to be only three ways to remedy it. (1) Actively abolish the habit of asking for illness and asking for medicine, and instead publish common sense questions and answers about various diseases in the publication, like the style recently published by Mr. Cheng Hanhua in the Shen Bao Medical Weekly. (2) As a passive method, add a prescribed scope to asking for illness and asking for medicine. Only certain minor diseases can solicit doctors' opinions by mail. And the statement in the letter must have at least a draft, arranged with several necessary items. The patient needs to fill it in completely before answering. (3) All question and answer columns on medical and pharmaceutical publications should be changed to consultant columns on health common sense and physiological common sense, but they should no longer use broad medical and pharmaceutical meanings.

Medical Musings 260

— Zhu Yang Gao

Talking about Immunity (Differences Between Young and Old)

We sometimes encounter other people's questions, saying whether the immunity (usually resistance) of young people (from newborns) is the same as that of older people? This issue is also often studied and discussed in serology, and the result can be said that the immunity of young people is weaker than that of older people. In newborns, it can almost be said that there is no immunity, that is, they can hardly resist pathogens that enter the body, and even if they have some resistance, it is very different from that of older people. Therefore, for the blood tests of infants, such as syphilis reactions, it is more appropriate to do them at least six months later. Otherwise, even if there is no toxic reaction, it is not enough to rely on it as a sign of no disease. Recently, some people have still been re-studying this issue (animal experiments), and the results are equal to the above, so I write about it. (Note that the above-mentioned immunity is specifically for automaticity, and the passive serum efficacy is the same in young and old.)

Talking about Friedmann's Tuberculosis Treatment Drug

FriedmimschesTuberculoseMittel

Friedmann's treatment is a kind of seedling slurry made according to immunological theory. Its ingredient is a kind of tuberculosis bacteria obtained from the body of a cold-blooded animal. Its intention is to enable the tuberculosis patients who have been vaccinated to produce a kind of resistance in their body and treat the tuberculosis in their body. Tuberculosis bacteria from cold-blooded animals have almost no toxicity to humans, so according to Friedmann's intention, there is absolutely no danger. His intention is very good, but the treatment results are not as good as his intention. In Europe and the United States, although there are many years of treatment experience, there are very few who praise its efficacy to this day. The reporter knows that it has also been discovered in Shanghai, so I report its recent results to those who are interested in this drug for reference.

Pulmonary tuberculosis expert Stedman treated 20 cases in the past two years. Among them, 50% were aggravated by using this drug, 25% did not change, and 25% were mild patients, so it was impossible to distinguish its effectiveness.

Notes on the Manufacture of Chinese Medicine 261

— Lin Hongzao

Preface

Our country's use of medicine to treat diseases dates back to ancient times. Shennong's tasting of hundreds of herbs marked the beginning of recorded Chinese medicine. Later generations compiled and wrote about it, and during the Ming Dynasty, Li Shizhen compiled the great compendium of Chinese medicine, the Compendium of Materia Medica. It contains no less than two thousand kinds of medicines, but it is criticized by the world for its theories of color, taste, the five elements, and their association with the internal organs. However, its unique effects are indeed amazing, and it is still praised by the world. Countries around the world are studying it and making every effort to adopt it. For example, ephedra is used as a treatment for asthma, and rhubarb is adopted into legal medicine, making a splash in the world and has long been well known. Furthermore, the production of angelica and coix seed into fine products shines brightly in today's pharmaceutical world. How can it not be said that Chinese medicine possesses these qualities? The inclusion of Chinese medicine in various national pharmacopoeias and other medical books is countless. Our country's lack of scientific progress has led to the shame of being supplanted by others. It is truly disheartening. If we do not quickly catch up and reform, they will take all our Chinese medicine and turn it into foreign medicine. However, Chinese medicine has more than two thousand kinds, and it is not easy to verify the ingredients of each one before using it. Therefore, we must take what they already know and use it as help from others. Examining scientific drugs, although there are many kinds, they can be roughly divided into three types, namely crude drugs, pure drugs, and preparations. Among these three, except for crude drugs that are directly used for their efficacy, pure drugs are ingredients extracted from crude drugs or chemical drugs. Their success is slow, and it is difficult to achieve results without considerable equipment and long-term research. Preparations are made by using crude drugs and their ingredients or chemical drugs, based on their efficacy, and using pharmaceutical science to make extracts, tinctures, and elixirs, to be used as needed for treatment. Although the manufacturing method is cumbersome, it is much more convenient than pure drugs. Moreover, due to its convenient application and durable storage, it occupies a leading position in pharmaceuticals. Why is the adoption of Chinese medicine not the same? The manufacture of rhubarb into tinctures and the refining of licorice into extracts are the most prominent examples. Our country is currently facing national difficulties and financial constraints. Is it possible to refine each Chinese medicine into pure drugs? Even the bark and roots of trees cannot be properly managed, let alone going against the grain. The preparation is easy to manufacture and is in line with the current improvement of Chinese medicine. If it can be refined into preparations based on known efficacy to alleviate urgent needs, it may not be a bad idea to assist Chinese medicine. This is the reason for writing this book. The preparations of Chinese medicine collected in the book are all those that have been adopted by various countries and used as lessons. Foreign medicines that can be replaced by Chinese medicines are also included for reference. As for the research on crude drugs and pure drugs of Chinese medicine, they will be discussed in separate books and are not within the scope of this book. I hope that the people of our country will rise up and conduct research and improvement. This is what the editor hopes. However, there may be omissions and errors, and I hope that scholars will correct them.

General Rules 262

(1) This book is divided into two sections. The first section is the general theory, discussing the techniques that preparations should have. The second section is the specific discussion, discussing the manufacturing methods of each preparation, with matters related to preparations attached at the end.

(2) The standards for the selection of each preparation in this book are as follows:

1. Those made purely with Chinese medicine,

2. Those that mix Chinese medicine with foreign medicine,

3. Those that can be replaced by Chinese medicine,

A total of three items are not limited to those already included in foreign pharmacopoeias, and those found in various pharmaceutical books are also included.

(3) Before the names of each preparation and the names of the drugs used in this book are finalized, the common names are temporarily translated and the original names are noted under the translated names for reference. Those that have been promulgated in the Chinese Pharmacopoeia shall follow them.

(4) The measurement system used in this book generally follows the convenience of each preparation, and the British and French systems are used in parallel. The system is described in another chapter.

(5) The dosage or extreme dosage of each preparation in this book is for adults. When applied to children or the elderly, it should be reduced according to age. However, if it is necessary to increase it for treatment, the physician shall be responsible for it based on experience and discretion. However, the pharmacist must carefully examine it and be responsible for rechecking it, and may only give it after inquiring with the prescribing physician.

(6) The classification of preparations should be listed according to their shape in pharmaceutical science. However, because the collections in this book are all Chinese medicines, for clarity, each preparation is listed after the corresponding Chinese medicine, with Chinese medicine as the main heading and preparations as the subheadings. (To be continued)

Common Sense Q&A About Diseases 263

— Cheng Hanzhang

(21) Emphysema and Atelectasis

(Q) What is emphysema?

(A) Emphysema is a state of abnormal expansion of the lungs due to excessive accumulation of air. It means that the lungs themselves are very expanded and have lost their elasticity.

(Q) What is atelectasis?

(A) This is the opposite of emphysema. The air content is very small or even completely absent, so the lungs themselves shrink.

(Q) How does emphysema occur?

(A) Most of them are caused by chronic bronchitis (inhalation of dust and tobacco, people who drink alcohol) and bronchial asthma, as well as repeated strong pressure on the lungs (playing the trumpet, glass blowers). But generally speaking, it seems to be related to physical constitution.

(Q) What are the symptoms of emphysema?

A The patient's chest expands, like a barrel, almost completely taking the posture of inhalation. The sternocleidomastoid muscle and scalene muscle are clearly prominent, the jugular vein is distended, the neck is short, the chest resistance increases, the respiratory movement is weak, and the vital capacity of the lungs is naturally reduced.

(Q) What symptoms can the doctor prove when percussing and auscultating?

(A) When percussing, there is a paper box sound, the lower border of the lung is lowered, and the mobility of the lung edge is reduced during breathing. During auscultation, the alveolar sound is weakened and the expiration is prolonged. There are also dry or wet rales.

(Q) What are the phenomena when taking X-rays?

(A) The lung area is very transparent, the diaphragm is flat, and the right ventricle must be enlarged.

(Q) Are there any changes in the heart?

(A) Yes. When percussing, the cardiac dullness area is reduced (this is because the lungs are covered). When auscultating, the heart sound is weak and the second pulmonic sound is strong.

(Q) What diseases are emphysema patients prone to?

(A) Prone to bronchitis.

(Q) What is the treatment for emphysema?

(A) Patients should avoid various causes, do not inhale dust, and move to a place with a good climate to completely cure chronic bronchitis. The medicine is expectorant such as tincture of ipecac, tincture of senega, ammonium chloride, etc. When there is a cough, you can use narcotic antitussives. When the heart is weak, use cardiotonics such as digitalis. For difficulty in breathing, mustard paste can be applied to the chest, and chest compression can be performed to help breathing.

(Q) What are the causes of atelectasis?

(A) There are congenital and acquired causes. The acquired causes are bronchial occlusion, compression of nearby organs, and weakening of respiratory muscles.

(Q) What are the symptoms of atelectasis?

(A) Acquired ones present with difficulty in breathing, the chest is depressed in an inspiratory shape, and the respiratory sound is weak and bronchial sounds, etc. are heard during auscultation.

(Q) How dangerous is this disease?

(A) Most congenital ones die. Acquired ones are not necessarily related to the cause and the breadth of the affected area.

(Q) What is the treatment for atelectasis?

(A) Pay attention to the cause and change the position. Use stimulants and tonics, and patients should take warm baths and deep breaths every day.

Free Talk

Reading "The Classic of Filial Piety" 264

— Cao Juren

I saw in the newspaper some time ago that a certain general ordered students to read "The Classic of Filial Piety." Recently, Dong, a resident of Funing, disobeyed his father, wrote a letter demanding money, called himself "Grand Old Man," and directly called his father by his name. The magistrate of Funing County detained Dong and ordered him to recite "The Classic of Filial Piety." This apocryphal book (Confucius's "ambition was in the Spring and Autumn Annals, and his actions were in the Classic of Filial Piety," see the Classic of Filial Piety Weigou Mingjue, which is not credible. Some say that the Classic of Filial Piety came from Zengzi, which is also not credible. Mencius called Zengzi's filial piety "cherishing his ambition," but there is no such statement in the Classic of Filial Piety. Mencius answered Gongduzi's question about Kuang Zhang's lack of filial piety, advocating "fathers and sons should not demand goodness from each other," which is also contrary to the Classic of Filial Piety's advocacy of "therefore, one should argue when there is injustice." This book was probably written by Confucian scholars in the early Han Dynasty and has nothing to do with Confucius, Mencius, or Zengzi. I suspect that the Classic of Filial Piety began with Zhu Xi, and Qing scholar Yao Jiheng has already made a conclusion.) is actually so popular this year. It is really beyond my expectations.

I have been familiar with the Classic of Filial Piety since I was a child, but I don't believe that this book will have any benefit to the world and people's hearts. After the Russo-Japanese War, Japanese elementary school students often formed groups to fight on the way home from school. During the European War, elementary school children often stabbed each other. These are all suggested by the hostility between countries and reflected in their psychology. In recent years, the various unethical phenomena in Chinese society are also a reflection of another kind of social phenomenon after careful examination. Since the late Qing Dynasty, the trend of vying for power has been greatly opened, and both openly and secretly, people are encouraged to lose their integrity and sell themselves. There is no such thing as integrity outside of speculation, and no such thing as morality outside of interests. In such a big upheaval, all ethical relations have been changed. The relationship between teachers and students, friends, brothers, and fathers and sons has naturally become a trading calculated on an abacus. On the other hand, due to the concept of personal enjoyment cultivated in cities, the sense of responsibility to the family has been reduced. Many old men and old ladies live under the eaves of their sons and daughters-in-law's small families, relying on their whims, and are not as good as servants. If it is said that disobedient children should read the Classic of Filial Piety, then there are many owners of modern small families who should read the Classic of Filial Piety today. Is it only Dong who should be detained?

Mr. Xiong Foxi once wrote a play about a foreign champion who called his "father an old comrade" and his "mother an old comrade." This foreign champion is not a fictional character. The foreign champion who returned from abroad feels that foreign ethics are all right and Chinese ethics are all in the way. He would rather be a loyal servant and errand boy for a "flying umbrella" than take responsibility for his old man. He would rather give his seat on the tram to an unfamiliar miss than let his old lady rest for a while. There are people who widely distribute the Treatise on Response of the Great Lord, but to no avail. The result of advising people to read the Classic of Filial Piety is probably the same.

The most important task at present is not to widely read the Classic of Filial Piety, but to encourage integrity and stop encouraging people to lose their integrity and sell themselves. This is the right way!

Sickness 265

— Jin Yi

That day when I got up in the morning, I felt that my head was heavy, as if it was no longer supported on my shoulders, but was drooping to the ground.

"I'm afraid I'm sick again!"

I sighed like a wisp of smoke.

"Any kind of hardship can be endured, but it's a bit difficult for a single person when they get sick!"

When I recalled what I said a long time ago, I shivered in alarm.

The sickness was obviously crawling on my body. My face was burning red, my jaw was too lazy to open, and I dragged my lazy steps wearily. I said to myself hatefully:

"It's better to die!"

Sitting in the chair, I wondered why I was sick again. So I thought of the unsettled dream last night. But isn't this too empty? Even if I'm not an unfeeling person, if I'm sick just because of the reappearance of a woman who has forgotten me in a dream, isn't it too ridiculous? But my head was dizzy, and I supported it with my hand.

Speaking of illness, I'm not afraid of it. Seeing people groaning in pain, I sincerely wished that I could suffer for that person. I can endure the harm that illness gives me, and so many times, it has not brought the last friend of mankind 丨丨 death.

My red face has always been said to be healthy, but they never thought that this healthy person has such a weak heart. This will be like my good friend, who can accompany me throughout my life. But this loyalty is also quite gratifying. Only under excessive melancholy and anger will it tell me to temporarily leave this world. But it always sends me back, letting me see that I am lying in someone's arms, or crawling up from the floor myself, touching the wounds on my face from falling.

I'm sick, and an irresistible cold comes from my heart. My body is shaking, my teeth are clattering, but I put on a scarf, put on a coat, and went out. I walked slowly, past one red door after another, struggling to walk up the arched bridge. Looking north, I saw the round tower in the North Sea against the blue sky, with its white color, standing there high and lonely. But looking down, floating on the beautiful green water, are all the scorched lotus leaves and lotus stalks!

I walked back as if I had gained something. I really felt that my head was too heavy, so I went back to bed.

All day long I didn't know if I was asleep or awake. Sometimes it seemed like there was a pair of eyes flashing in front of me, but they were gone immediately. I don't know where I am, and I don't know where to go.

Dusk, slid down from the wings of crows. When I opened my eyes and looked at the gradually darkening house, it was already time to turn on the lights, but I couldn't stand up. I turned over sadly, and I couldn't help but shed tears for this feeling of loneliness.

But a friend with the heart of a child came in, and he asked me kindly, putting his hand on my burning forehead.

I sighed deeply.

My illness quietly left after making me endure a day of pain. In this way, I stood up healthily again, writing with a pen or speaking with my mouth: I can be a bachelor, I can live peacefully by myself. But I only hope that illness is my most unfamiliar guest.

Literary Miscellany (Continued) 266

— Meng Yuan

(3)

In the "Suzhou-Shanghai Exchange" section of the fifth issue of the second volume of "Literary Tea Party," Mr. Sun Fuxi said that he visited Tianping Mountain in Suzhou. One of the impressions he got in the "painted boat" was:

Most of the sedan chair carriers in Suzhou are women, so they can be called sedan chair women. Their courageous and hardworking spirit is really admirable. However, the petty haggling over prices and asking for money for wine, snacks, and straw sandals (I don't recognize this word, and there is no dictionary to look up, so please forgive me for not noting it! Meng) really lowers this hardworking spirit a lot.

Meng Yuan said: This is "chrysanthemum philosophy." The philosophy that is named "chrysanthemum" means "purity and loftiness." For example, Suzhou women can be "courageous and hardworking." If they tighten their stomachs and don't want money, then wouldn't the impression given to "tourists" be better and more unified? And asking for money, and asking for it endlessly, this naturally makes people change from the "admirable" position to the sigh of "spiritual degradation." After hearing Mr. Sun's words, I don't know if Suzhou women can change their ways and never eat from now on, and never ask for money for carrying sedan chairs from now on?

A Brief Reply to Mr. Xu Maoyong 267

— Shi Heng

Mr. Maoyong:

Because the editor of "Free Talk" is unwilling to take up space with this issue, it is very difficult to see Mr. X's letter, and it is necessary to briefly reply a sentence or two. Mr. X brought up the divergence between idealism and materialism in art theory, which in my opinion is not the case at all. What I have repeatedly said is to make Mr. X first recognize the truth of art, and then talk about the truth of society or the truth of history. This theoretical step is not based on the different viewpoints of idealism or materialism. Without looking far, G, the author of "The Iron Flood", and Nie La Tuofu, cannot be said to be an idealist in any case, but he cannot completely abandon the truth of art and discuss the historical truth of "The Iron Flood". I think one of the main differences between idealism and materialism is that one only takes the truth of art as the complete purpose, and the other takes the truth of art as a means to achieve the truth of society or history. If so, wouldn't it be wrong for Mr. X to call me an idealist! As for "Shaning", we all agree that it is historically untrue, but I say that its untruth is quite related to its artistic untruth. However, Mr. X initially denied this step, but in this last letter, Mr. X can say: "I have never placed the expression of art in a position secondary to the recognition of reality." Then what is there to argue about?

Mr. X pointed out where I misunderstood, but I still cannot admit it. According to Mr. X's mechanical view of art, although it does not go so far as to identify Don Quixote as a knight and Hamlet as a Danish prince, for the mechanical method used to combine artistic characters with social existence, the result is still an equal fallacy.

If Mr. X still insists that I am an idealist, I hope Mr. X can give me a detailed analysis, and I am also willing to learn and correct myself. But I cannot accept the principle of "social existence" that determines art!

I admit that this issue can now be concluded. If no new issues are raised, I have decided not to answer any more, because I want to save the space of "Free Talk". Please forgive me for not being polite.

Two Brothers (62) 268

— Guy de Maupassant, translated by Li Weikehui

She couldn't help but burst into anger when she heard this. The word turtle was too unpleasant, and she thought it was indirectly mocking her.

"Who are you saying that to?"

"To Zhe'an! It's really funny to see them like that!"

She was so moved that she shuddered slightly and muttered in a low voice:

"Ah, Pierre, how cruel you are! This woman is the embodiment of integrity. Your brother will never find anyone better than her."

He simply burst out laughing, a deliberate, sudden laugh.

"Ha! Ha! Ha! The embodiment of integrity! All women are the embodiment of integrity... and all their husbands are turtles. Ha! Ha! Ha!"

She didn't say a word, stood up, hurriedly ran down the sloping sandy beach, risking slipping and falling into those holes hidden under the grass, breaking her legs or arms, and went straight, almost running, through those muddy roads, towards her other son.

When Zhe'an saw her approaching, he shouted:

"What's wrong? Mom, have you decided to come catch shrimp?"

She didn't answer him, grabbed his arm, as if to say to him: "Save me, protect me!"

He was taken aback when he saw her so flustered;

"Your face is so pale! What's wrong with you?"

She stammered:

"I almost fell, I walked through these reefs with trepidation."

So Zhe'an guided her, helped her, and told her about the methods of catching shrimp, in order to arouse her interest in this matter. But because she didn't pay attention to his words at all, and he felt a strong urge to tell someone his secret, he took her to a farther place and said to her in a low voice:

"Guess what I did?"

"But... but... I don't know."

"Guess."

"I... I don't know."

"Then I'll tell you, I told Mrs. Lu that I wanted to marry her."

She didn't answer anything. Her head was buzzing and she almost didn't understand his words. She repeated:

"Marry her?"

"That's right, did I do well? She's very cute, isn't she?"

"Yes... very cute... you did well."

"Then do you agree?"

"Yes... I agree."

"You look so strange when you say that. Others think... think... you're dissatisfied."

"But I... I'm satisfied."

"Really?"

In order to prove that she was indeed satisfied, she hugged him tightly and kissed him on the face, a heavy kiss from a mother to her child.

After she wiped away the few tears that welled up in her eyes, she saw a person sleeping face down on the beach over there, like a corpse, his face buried in the sand. This was her other son, Pierre, who was thinking hard and despairing.

So she took her little Zhe'an and walked farther away, to a place very close to the waves. They talked for a long time about this marriage, which was her greatest concern.

The rising tide drove them to join the other shrimp catchers, and afterwards everyone returned to shore, waking up Pierre, who was pretending to be asleep. The dinner that day lasted a long time. Everyone drank a lot of wine.
